1. An exceptional location, Check.
2. A warm and inviting atmosphere, Check.
3. Professionals intent on making you comfortable, Check.

5. They make you look freaking good!!!! Check.

I have never had such a horrible experience in a salon.  I went to Kim Brown, who rents a booth there, and only learned of the name she bills under by the receipt sent to me via e-mail.  I then looked up reviews on her and they were horrible.  But the reviews for Frederick Michael Salon are not but they are not about her.  My hair was longer on one side than the other and I asked her to fix it.  She agreed and when I got there I said that I had never paid so much for a color and cut ($225.00) and thought I should love my hair.  She immediately started to defend herself and proceeded to start screaming at me.  By that time I didn't want her to do anything to my hair and told her I had read bad reviews about her but did not have the information to check them before coming in.  She told me I was creepy and not to come back.  I was shocked at the manner in which she behaved.  There was a man working in the attic above the room she rents in the salon and he met me out in the hallway after she slammed the door in my face.  He looked for the owner but he was not there.  I wanted to dispute the charges for the first time in my life (and I am 62 years old) but I will go to someone else and eat the charges.  I would be afraid of physical violence from a person like that.  If you call and they send you to her, STAY AWAY.</text>

< Review>
This is a small store in the Elmwood neighborhood with some amazing chocolate bars!  If your a fan of a little spice, some of their chocolate has a wonderful little bit of heat to it.  The Chili mango bars have candied mange along with a bit of chili in them.   The Mole bars have a few spices giving it the flavor of mole and a hint of heat!  These are wonderful.   They also have non spicy chocolate with wondeful accents and flavors.    If you like hot chocolate, be sure to try the hot chocolate with a bit of cinnamon and I believe vanilla, thick and creamy!! Wonderful on these cold rainy days.<//Review>

Their chocolate bars are very inventive, combining great chocolate with South American flavors â€“ I highly recommend their recent addition, the Fuerte bar. Itâ€™s topped with roasted quinoa, pepitas (pumpkin seeds), almonds, chili flakes and sea salt. I also crave their luscious chocolate cupcakes regularly â€“ they also have a deal with these: you get a discount if you bring back their little cupcake box for a refill. They can point you towards their vegan offerings, almost everything is gluten free, and they donâ€™t use gelatin. Very friendly staff and chocolate bar samples always available!

Iâ€™m giving them 4/5 â€œgreen starsâ€ for social and environmental impact. They are a Latina-owned business that aims to make delicious chocolates using sustainable ingredients. From their website: â€œwe aim to purchase the chocolate from chocolate purveyors who have a direct relationship with cocoa farmers.  We believe that direct trade with cocoa farmers results in farmers making far more than Fair Trade standards.â€ But when they opened in 2012, they purchased pre-made chocolate from Guittard, which is somewhat confusing since Guittard do use the official Fair Trade certification system. Most of their chocolate is a South American blend and in some cases they use single origin chocolate (the Quechua bar is Ecuadorian chocolate). In an interview, chocolatier Arcelia Gallardo says that â€œeventually we want to work with smaller cacao farmers and chocolate makersâ€ but it has been 4 years since they opened, so itâ€™s time they provided an update on their chocolate sourcing â€“ are they still mainly buying from Guittard or are they starting to trade directly with smaller farmers? Not that Guittard is a bad company â€“ most of their cacao is Fair Trade and shade grown; some is organic. Casa de Chocolates donâ€™t mention if any of their cacao is organically grown but the staff member I talked to said sheâ€™d find out, so Iâ€™ll update that when I go back.

Most of their other ingredients are organic: milk, cream, eggs, butter, flour, confectionersâ€™ sugar, espresso beans, berries and herbs. <text>If I could give them more than five stars, I would! Let's start with the artists. Jacob (check out his instagram @jdanhi) did my tattoo and he is a phenomenal tattoo artist who's an expert when it comes to shading. But every artist at Third Street Tattoo is amazing. Each offers a distinctive style of tattooing and can tailor their style to fit your vision.

Their customer service also met and went beyond my expectations. I was there for seven hours getting my tattoo. During that time, I saw how they really did their best to accommodate every single walk in that came through. Plus, they really do try to take care of you. Because of how long my tattoo session was, there were definitely times where I needed to take a break, and Jacob was more than happy to give me all the time I needed. At a couple points, I started feeling really nauseous, which isn't surprising considering how long I was getting tattooed. When I mentioned it, everyone was super helpful. They offered snacks, water and allowed me to lie down for a while until it passed. I don't think I could have finished getting my tattoo if they weren't so understanding, helpful, and patient!

If you're looking to get a tattoo, check this place out! I could not be happier with how it looks and with their customer service.</text>< username>

<review>Right off the bat I will take some of the responsibility for not being happy with my tattoo. I have two existing half-sleeves as well as another tattoo, so I do have a little knowledge about having work done. About three weeks ago I went in based on a recommendation to have the initials of two family members who've passed tattooed on the inside of my wrist done in fine line. When I explained what I wanted to the gentleman behind the counter, he replied "no problem" but came back a few minutes later and asked if I would mind having a "guest artist" do the work (mistake number one). I agreed and spoke to the person who was going to do the work. We went back and forth over size and fonts but he kept drawing the initials too large. I asked him repeatedly to make them smaller but he simply replied "it can't be done" (mistake number two). We finally agreed on the size and font and he set to work. He certainly was polite enough, seemed competent, I paid for the tat ($100 for six letters) and left. Three weeks later I now seriously regret letting a "guest artist" work on me. The lines aren't sharp at all, I definitely wouldn't consider it to be fine line work and there's a halo effect around all the letters. Maybe he had too much caffeine that morning, who knows? The bottom line is that I am now looking at laser removal procedures in hopes that most (if not all) the damage can be rectified so I can have someone competent do the work. As mentioned earlier, I have two half-sleeves and both of them have very fine lines that still remain sharp almost 16 years later. Sorry guys but my guess is you let someone who's just starting out mess up the work on one of your customers. You may want to screen your "guess artists" a little more thoroughly in the future.</review>< Pictures>

<UserId.>106662344045469412664</UserId.><user_name>James Barros<//user_name><Date>1597077144408< /Date>< Rate>

<Text>I signed up for Skydive Elsinore's "Accelerated Freefall Level 1" in part because I'm terrified of heights, and in part because my friend was and I didn't want him to go alone.  (AFF means you jump with an instructor on either side, but you are jumping yourself, controlling yourself, and land your own parachute, vs a tandem jump where the instructor is strapped to you and can handle any aspects of the jump you don't want to)

The campus is cool.  There's definitely a "bro" vibe, but it's not overpowering. Everyone is super friendly and excited.  Everyone is willing to answer questions and wants to help, from instructors to random jumpers.

Once you get into classroom, the facility gets very professional and it reminded me of a more intimate, more friendly Army classroom.

The instructors were patient and detail oriented.  We drilled a LOT on the ground, including how to handle every conceivable type of emergency, with a lot of visual aids and exercises which left me confident I could get safely to ground no matter what happened. We even practiced exit procedures from what I think may have been the real tail sections of decommissioned planes.

The aircraft I went up in felt very new (and even had modern avionics, which I was not expecting at all)

In the air, even though I had poor body position the instructors kept me on track and were re-assuring, friendly, supportive and professional.

The landing pattern which seemed scary and narrow when I was on the ground looking at maps was super easy to navigate from the air and landing, just like all the in-air exercises were very easy because the instructors had taken their time to drill the process over and over on the ground.

I can not think of a single complaint. I am over the moon happy with Skydive Elsinore and give them an unqualified recommendation.</Text><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNnxzBEk5dnvZc3U7m7YK2BSA_K22b01ucVQXca=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pictures>< response>

<review>Skydiving was probably one of the BEST things i've ever done in my entire life! I came here to celebrate my friends 21st birthday and after two weeks of contemplating this once in a lifetime opportunity to skydive I probably would have never thought of actually going haha!!. It was a group of us and our appointment was set at 11 A.M. however, the sky was very cloudy that day so therefore we had to wait a couple of hours to see if the clouds would clear up. I was very optimistic that we were gonna skydive that day ! Shout out to the guy we met there named Stake! He gave us a tour around the grounds (only because it was very cloudy and it was a high chance that we weren't going to be able to skydive due to weather). He showed us the airplanes and just told us what to expect when we were going to jump hahaha! After a couple hours of waiting the sun began to come out and the clouds started to clear up and it was showtime !! Justin (super funny dude) was my skydive instructor and I cannot thank him enough for making my first skydive experience so much fun! He kept ensuring me that everything was gonna go smooth and he was very knowledgeable about skydiving and he told me everything I have to do to make this go well. Honestly I wasn't as nervous as I was days before but I was just so ready to experience this thrill! Justin made sure that I was secure and as soon as we were getting ready to get on the plane, he told me that we were going first haha. Skydiving is not as scary as people might think it is, however the experience is probably different for every person but thanks to all the friendly and professional staff for making this experience memorable I will definitely come back with my family !!  Thank you so much Beth (I think that is her name), Justin, the camera guy (I forgot his name lol)  and Stake for making this experience so AMAZING!!< /review>< date>

<userid>111346022810647046969</userid><Name>Ray Holt</Name>< Text>
I used to skydive in the 80s & 90s, we took my son for a tandem jump for his 18th birthday and we had a blast.  The instructors are awesome, all top notch professionals with many years of experience.

I think everyone should jump once, maybe 2 times because you only get 50-60 seconds of free fall time.  Skydiving is one of the safest sports out there with 1 death per 1,000,000 jumps.  There aren't many sports with that safety record except maybe checkers.

Do it once, you'll never regret it.</Text>

Great first time everyone was friendly yet professional. I really appreciated tandem jumper Joe, made the experience comfortable and fun. I wasn't scared or second guessing at all but i got the feeling if i was joe woulda been the dude to get me to go through with it. 2 things they dont tell you worth noting, first a minor pounding pain in your head till your ears are able to pop and even then it takes about 15 mins to hear normally. <user>107107696849530149991< /user>< username>
Beatrixbelle</username>
<date>1446858117423<//date><Rating>5<//Rating>< Review>
This was my first time skydiving. I'd heard before that skydiving is a "hurry up and wait" kind of experience, so I was prepared for it. I made my appointment for 11/2 at 9 am, but I showed up at 8:30. (It's just always better to have the extra cushion of time.) What you need to understand first off is that your safety is in their hands, and they have a lot of factors to contend with - wind/weather conditions, properly securing the equipment, seeing to every jumper, and yes, the paperwork, because if you haven't heard, Americans are kind of litigious, and they have to cover their bases. So you likely won't be going up right on time. I, myself didn't get geared up until closer to 10, but hey, if that's the cost of me safely landing from a 12,500 foot drop, then that's fine by me!
I was lucky to get Marcelo as my instructor - he immediately made me feel right at ease with everything. He was very friendly, personable, and positive. Even with the plane at the full altitude, I wasn't anxious like I thought I would be. And the jump? Well, you'd just have to try it for yourself to know what it's really like! In Elsinore, you see it all - the desert, the mountains, and the sea. It was an incredible experience, and I will definitely be doing it again. I am so glad I came here for my first jump!<//Review>

The first time I went I had a wonderful time but my DVD that I purchased was scratched. Fast forward 7 years and I go to skydive again. The experience is 5 stars, but the quality of the video I got was so incredibly poor. I was incredibly disappointed because there is no way they can redo it unless I jump again, which, physically, I can't. The guy doing the photography and videotaping had the sun in the background the duration of my jump so you can't even see anything except a speck against the sun. He never got close enough so one would never know who or what even jumped out of the plane, let alone knowing that it's me. I paid extra for the DVD and photos and regardless that the cameraman isn't a professional, he could at least have the knowledge to know that you should be able to SEE the person you are filming. My friend who jumped with me also paid extra and while their video game it great, it took Skydive Elsinore over a week to send it. Claiming that they had sent it when in reality they never did. It's supposed to be received within 48 hours. All in all, at least the most important part, the jump, was perfect.<//text>

It was my Dads 60th so we got him a skydiving trip, my wife and a close family friend all went with him.  The original day we went was too cloudy we had to reschedule , which was a breeze to do with the very friendly and helpful staff. Today we went and the staff was great very social and really pumped it up to make it fun, I have to say that Jared was a shining star and just his energy made me want to sign up, but then I realized I was a chicken. we did the video package everything was great, our good friend had a rough landing where she didn't get her feet up and it looks like she broke her ankle. 3</rate>
<Text>Skydive Elsinore provides a very unique experience for those willing to be hurled out of an aircraft and into a freefall. Their staff are well qualified, and know what they are doing.

From a critical perspective, it appears that scheduling could be managed a little better. Our early morning schedule which was purchased in advance was delayed and we, along with other tandem jumpers waited approximately 5 hours before the jump. The wait was not due to weather, or mechanical delays, as group after group went ahead. When inquiring about the status of the assigned jump the typical answer given was "about thirty more minutes" which degraded into uncertainty.

It could be that this situation was rare.

Overall, you'll enjoy the experience, but be prepared to wait just in case it turns into an unexpectedly long day.< /Text><Pictures>None</Pictures>< Response>

< text>
I love Skydive Elsinore! It's such a friendly dz, helpful staff, good amenities, and great jumping for both experienced and new jumpers.  The views while skydiving are brilliant and good to capture on video.  Lots of coaching available for all levels to build or refine their skills. Kit store, bar, snack bar, bunks and showers on site, think there's rv hook-up available too. We've been coming here since 2001 and this place never disappoints. The staff can cater for solo jumpers or teams and various British teams regularly hold expeds here.</text>

<userid>103319749644454200519</userid>< Text>
Easy process. Nice people. Lots of fun. I took my son for his 18th birthday. He was not feeling well and we got through the whole process waiting to get on the plane. He wanted to jump do badly I could not convince him to come back another day until his headache was so bad he decided to reschedule. Lake Elsinore Skydiving made it super easy to reschedule.  I just called them up when we were ready a few weeks later and we showed up. The instructors were nice. Only issue is waiting around not knowing how long is going to take to get to from start to finish. They tell you it would be a two to four hour process. That kind of kills your day and any plans. Lots of fun nonetheless. My son had an awesome time. My ears started hurting super bad with the altitude change on the freefall. They're still plugged up. Another young man in the plane said the same thing when we were finishing up. Not sure how to change that or what to recommend for someone else, just know there's a possibility this may occur.</Text>

<user_name>Edmond Dantes</user_name><Time>1465196135723< /Time>< rate>
5<//rate>
<review>I'm an AFF student and had my first jumps yesterday.

Ground coach: Lindsay
AFF Level 1: Luca & Brodie
AFF Level 2: Luca & Cory

First off the staff are all AMAZING people. Fun, enjoyable, and super professional when it comes to "safety" and training.

I trust my life with these individuals and have complete confidence in their skills and abilities simply because of the fact that they know what the hell they are doing and have the jumps to prove it.

The facility is pretty nice and I really liked the metal work throughout the entire place. There's a stainless steel logo in the office and the welds blew my mind. Clean bathrooms and showers. Nice shaded area to chill.

***ADVICE FOR AFF LEVEL 1 STUDENTS***
PLAN AHEAD ON STAYING 2 DAYS just in case.

Personally, as a student, I think it's better to make a weekend out of it whenever you visit Skydive Elsinore. There's a lot to learn and trying learn anything after a 2 hour commute is daunting.

This isn't like getting a Bachelor's Degree. There's no "pass and forget" so make sure you are fresh and ready soak in the important info and be ready to drill it in! 100% commitment.

In retrospect, I thought it was a more beneficial to the learning process to have the ground class, sleep on it, study, and be rested and alert for the next day.

Lastly, after everything is checked and rechecked, the wind still determines who jumps. The entire facility can be grounded if the weather is bad.

Levels 2-8 do not take that long and neither do the solos. You can easily get multiple jumps completed in 1 day; however, staying that extra day and keeping a track of the weather before you go will maximize your chances of getting your jumps in.

Do not schedule things too far in advance because the weather can change. You have to be flexible.

One thing not listed on their website is that they offer wind tunnel training with a coach. If you are between Levels 3 and 4 it is a great option to explore<//review>< pictures>
None< /pictures>
